   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><span dir="auto">New York University</span></h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent"> 
    <div id="siteSub">

    </div>

      This article is about the private Manhattan-based university. For a list of universities in New York, see 
      <a href="/wiki/Universities_in_New_York" title="Universities in New York" class="mw-redirect">Universities in New York</a>.

     <p><b>New York University</b> (<b>NYU</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nonsectarian" title="Nonsectarian">nonsectarian</a> American <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">research</a> university based in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. NYU's main campus is situated in the <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a>. Founded in 1831, NYU is one of the largest private <a href="/wiki/Nonprofit_institution" title="Nonprofit institution" class="mw-redirect">nonprofit institutions</a> of American <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-schools_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schools-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-schools_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schools-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The university counts 36 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="Nobel laureates by university affiliation" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Prize winners</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Abel_Prize" title="Abel Prize">Abel Prize winners</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> 10 <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a> recipients,<sup id="cite_ref-philanthropy_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-philanthropy-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyu_a_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyu_a-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> 16 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners,<sup id="cite_ref-collegecrunch.org_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collegecrunch.org-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> 30 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> winners,<sup id="cite_ref-collegecrunch.org_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collegecrunch.org-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYU_Oscars_2011_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_Oscars_2011-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYU_Emmys_2011_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_Emmys_2011-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> four <a href="/wiki/Putnam_Competition" title="Putnam Competition" class="mw-redirect">Putnam Competition</a> winners, <a href="/wiki/Russ_Prize" title="Russ Prize">Russ Prize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Prize" title="Gordon Prize">Gordon Prize</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Draper_Prize" title="Draper Prize" class="mw-redirect">Draper Prize</a> winners, <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a> winners, and <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony Award</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> winners among its faculty and alumni. NYU also has <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows_Program" title="MacArthur Fellows Program">MacArthur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Fellowship" title="Guggenheim Fellowship">Guggenheim Fellowship</a> holders<sup id="cite_ref-guggenheim_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guggenheim-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a> members among its past and present <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_University_alumni" title="List of New York University alumni">graduates</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_University_faculty_and_staff" title="List of New York University faculty and staff">faculty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-facultyhandbook_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facultyhandbook-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU is organized into 18 schools, colleges, and institutes,<sup id="cite_ref-schools_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schools-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> located in six centers throughout <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Brooklyn" title="Downtown Brooklyn">Downtown Brooklyn</a>, as well as more than a dozen other sites across the world, with plans for further expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-abu_dhabi_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abu_dhabi-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_International_Education" title="Institute of International Education">Institute of International Education</a>, NYU sends more students to study abroad than any other US college or university, and the <a href="/wiki/College_Board" title="College Board">College Board</a> reports more online searches by international students for &quot;NYU&quot; than for any other university.<sup id="cite_ref-NYU_overseas_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_overseas-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table id="toc" class="toc">

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_University" title="History of New York University">History of New York University</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Albert_Gallatin_3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Albert_Gallatin_3.JPG/170px-Albert_Gallatin_3.JPG" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Albert_Gallatin_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Albert_Gallatin_3.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Albert_Gallatin_3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Albert_Gallatin" title="Albert Gallatin">Albert Gallatin</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Albert_Gallatin" title="Albert Gallatin">Albert Gallatin</a>, Secretary of Treasury under <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a>, declared his intention to establish &quot;in this immense and fast-growing city ... a system of rational and practical education fitting for all and graciously opened to all&quot;. A three-day long &quot;literary and scientific convention&quot; held in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Hall" title="New York City Hall">City Hall</a> in 1830 and attended by over 100 delegates debated the terms of a plan for a new university. These New Yorkers believed the city needed a university designed for young men who would be admitted based on merit, not birthright, status or social class. On April 18, 1831, an institution was established, with the support of a group of prominent New York City residents from the city's landed class of <a href="/wiki/Merchant" title="Merchant">merchants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banker" title="Banker" class="mw-redirect">bankers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trader_(finance)" title="Trader (finance)">traders</a>. Albert Gallatin was elected as the institution's first president. On April 21, 1831, the new institution received its <a href="/wiki/Charter" title="Charter">charter</a> and was incorporated as the University of the City of New York by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Legislature" title="New York State Legislature">New York State Legislature</a>; older documents often refer to it by that name. The university has been popularly known as New York University since its beginning and was officially renamed New York University in 1896. In 1832, NYU held its first classes in rented rooms of four-story Clinton Hall, situated near <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Hall" title="New York City Hall">City Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-archives1_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archives1-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1835, the <a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Law" title="NYU School of Law" class="mw-redirect">School of Law</a>, NYU's first professional school, was established. Although the impetus to found a new school was partly a reaction by <a href="/wiki/Evangelical" title="Evangelical" class="mw-redirect">evangelical</a> <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" title="Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect">Presbyterians</a> to what they perceived as the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopalianism</a> of <a href="/wiki/Columbia_College,_Columbia_University" title="Columbia College, Columbia University">Columbia College</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-gotham_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gotham-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU was created <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational" title="Non-denominational">non-denominational</a>, unlike many American colleges at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-archives1_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archives1-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Nyuuniheights.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Nyuuniheights.jpg/220px-Nyuuniheights.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Nyuuniheights.jpg/330px-Nyuuniheights.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Nyuuniheights.jpg/440px-Nyuuniheights.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Nyuuniheights.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The University Heights campus, now home to the 
        <a href="/wiki/Bronx_Community_College" title="Bronx Community College">Bronx Community College</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Whereas NYU had its <a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_Park" title="Washington Square Park">Washington Square</a> campus since its founding, the university purchased a campus at <a href="/wiki/University_Heights,_Bronx" title="University Heights, Bronx">University Heights</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">the Bronx</a> because of overcrowding on the old campus. NYU also had a desire to follow New York City's development further uptown. NYU's move to the Bronx occurred in 1894, spearheaded by the efforts of Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Henry_Mitchell_MacCracken" title="Henry Mitchell MacCracken" class="mw-redirect">Henry Mitchell MacCracken</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-archives1_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archives1-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The University Heights campus was far more spacious than its predecessor was. As a result, most of the university's operations along with the undergraduate <a href="/wiki/NYU_College_of_Arts_and_Science" title="NYU College of Arts and Science" class="mw-redirect">College of Arts and Science</a> and School of Engineering were housed there. NYU's administrative operations were moved to the new campus, but the graduate schools of the university remained at Washington Square.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1914, Washington Square College was founded as the downtown undergraduate college of NYU. In 1935, NYU opened the &quot;Nassau College-Hofstra Memorial of New York University at Hempstead, Long Island&quot;. This extension would later become a fully independent <a href="/wiki/Hofstra_University" title="Hofstra University">Hofstra University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the late 1960s and early 1970s, financial crisis gripped the New York City government and the troubles spread to the city's institutions, including NYU.<sup id="cite_ref-nyuandvillage_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyuandvillage-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Feeling the pressures of imminent bankruptcy, NYU President <a href="/wiki/James_McNaughton_Hester" title="James McNaughton Hester">James McNaughton Hester</a> negotiated the sale of the University Heights campus to the <a href="/wiki/City_University_of_New_York" title="City University of New York">City University of New York</a>, which occurred in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> After the sale of the Bronx campus, University College merged with Washington Square College. In the 1980s, under the leadership of President <a href="/wiki/John_Brademas" title="John Brademas">John Brademas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU launched a billion-dollar campaign that was spent almost entirely on updating facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The campaign was set to complete in 15 years, but ended up being completed in 10.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003 President <a href="/wiki/John_Sexton" title="John Sexton">John Sexton</a> launched a $2.5 billion campaign for funds to be spent especially on faculty and financial aid resources.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_logo">University logo</span></h3> 
     <p>The university logo, the upheld torch, is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty" title="Statue of Liberty">Statue of Liberty</a>, signifying NYU's service to the city of New York. The torch is depicted on both the NYU seal and the more abstract NYU logo, designed in 1965 by renowned graphic designer <a href="/wiki/Tom_Geismar" title="Tom Geismar">Tom Geismar</a> of the branding and design firm <a href="/wiki/Chermayeff_%26_Geismar" title="Chermayeff &amp; Geismar" class="mw-redirect">Chermayeff &amp; Geismar</a>. There are at least two versions of the possible origin of the university color, <a href="/wiki/Violet_(color)" title="Violet (color)">violet</a>. Some believe that it may have been chosen because <a href="/wiki/Violet_(plant)" title="Violet (plant)" class="mw-redirect">violets</a> are said to have grown abundantly in Washington Square and around the buttresses of the Old University Building. Others argue that the color may have been adopted because the violet was the flower associated with <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, the center of learning in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greece</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-facultyhandbook_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facultyhandbook-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_setting">Cultural setting</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_Park" title="Washington Square Park">Washington Square</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a> have been hubs of <a href="/wiki/Cultural_learning" title="Cultural learning">cultural life</a> in New York City since the early 19th century. Much of this culture has intersected with NYU at various points in its history. <a href="/wiki/Artist" title="Artist">Artists</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River_School" title="Hudson River School">Hudson River School</a>, the United States' first prominent school of painters, settled around Washington Square. <a href="/wiki/Samuel_F.B._Morse" title="Samuel F.B. Morse" class="mw-redirect">Samuel F.B. Morse</a>, the first chair of Painting and Sculpture at NYU, and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Huntington" title="Daniel Huntington">Daniel Huntington</a> were early tenants of the Old University Building in the mid-19th century. (The University rented out studio space and residential apartments within the &quot;academic&quot; building.) Artists and <a href="/wiki/Intellectual" title="Intellectual">intellectuals</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe">Edgar Allan Poe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain" title="Mark Twain">Mark Twain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herman_Melville" title="Herman Melville">Herman Melville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Walt_Whitman" title="Walt Whitman">Walt Whitman</a>, have contributed to the artistic scene encompassing NYU. As a result, they had notable interaction with the cultural and academic life of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-nyuandvillage_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyuandvillage-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the 1870s, sculptors <a href="/wiki/Augustus_Saint-Gaudens" title="Augustus Saint-Gaudens">Augustus Saint-Gaudens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Chester_French" title="Daniel Chester French">Daniel Chester French</a> lived and worked near the Square. By the 1920s, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_Park" title="Washington Square Park">Washington Square Park</a> was nationally recognized as a focal point for artistic and moral rebellion. As such, the Washington Square campus became more diverse and bustled with urban energy, contributing to academic change at NYU.<sup id="cite_ref-nyuandvillage_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyuandvillage-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Famed residents of this time include <a href="/wiki/Eugene_O%27Neill" title="Eugene O'Neill">Eugene O'Neill</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Sloan" title="John Sloan" class="mw-redirect">John Sloan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Prendergast" title="Maurice Prendergast">Maurice Prendergast</a>. In the 1930s, the abstract expressionists <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Pollock" title="Jackson Pollock">Jackson Pollock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willem_de_Kooning" title="Willem de Kooning">Willem de Kooning</a>, and the realists <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hopper" title="Edward Hopper">Edward Hopper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hart_Benton_(painter)" title="Thomas Hart Benton (painter)">Thomas Hart Benton</a> had studios around Washington Square. In the 1960s the area became one of the centers of the beat and folk generation, when <a href="/wiki/Allen_Ginsberg" title="Allen Ginsberg">Allen Ginsberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a> settled there. This led to tension with the university, which at the time was in the midst of an aggressive facilities expansion phase.<sup id="cite_ref-nyuandvillage_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyuandvillage-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1975, the university opened The Grey Art Gallery at 100 Washington Square East, housing the New York University art collection and featuring museum quality exhibitions.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Campus_of_New_York_University" title="Campus of New York University">Campus of New York University</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Most of NYU's buildings are located across a roughly 229-acre (930,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) area bounded by <a href="/wiki/Houston_Street" title="Houston Street">Houston Street</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(New_York_City)" title="Broadway (New York City)">Broadway</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/14th_Street_(Manhattan)" title="14th Street (Manhattan)">14th Street</a> to the north, and <a href="/wiki/Sixth_Avenue_(Manhattan)" title="Sixth Avenue (Manhattan)">Sixth Avenue</a> (Avenue of the Americas) to the west. The core of NYU consists of buildings that surround <a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_Park" title="Washington Square Park">Washington Square Park</a>.</p> 
     <p>With approximately 12,500 residents, NYU has the seventh-largest university housing system in the U.S. as of 2007, and one of the largest among private schools.<sup id="cite_ref-housingranking_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-housingranking-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_Square_campus">Washington Square campus</span></h3> 
     <p>Since the late 1970s, the central part of NYU has been its Washington Square campus in the heart of <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_Arch" title="Washington Square Arch">Washington Square Arch</a> is an unofficial symbol of NYU. Until 2007, NYU had held its commencement ceremonies in Washington Square Park, but moved the ceremonies to <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a> in 2008 because of renovations to Washington Square.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Main_buildingNYU.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Main_buildingNYU.JPG/220px-Main_buildingNYU.JPG" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Main_buildingNYU.JPG/330px-Main_buildingNYU.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/94/Main_buildingNYU.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Main_buildingNYU.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Silver_Center" title="Silver Center">Silver Center</a> c. 1900
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the 1990s, NYU became a &quot;two square&quot; university by building a second community around <a href="/wiki/Union_Square_(New_York_City)" title="Union Square (New York City)">Union Square</a>, in close proximity to Washington Square. NYU's Union Square community primarily consists of the priority residence halls of Carlyle Court, <a href="/wiki/Palladium_(New_York_City)" title="Palladium (New York City)">Palladium</a> Residence Hall, Alumni Hall, Coral Tower, Thirteenth Street Hall, University Hall, Third North Residence Hall, and Founders Hall.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_student_works_on_Rube-Goldberg_part_at_Tisch_Ctr_for_Arts.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NYU_student_works_on_Rube-Goldberg_part_at_Tisch_Ctr_for_Arts.JPG/220px-NYU_student_works_on_Rube-Goldberg_part_at_Tisch_Ctr_for_Arts.JPG" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NYU_student_works_on_Rube-Goldberg_part_at_Tisch_Ctr_for_Arts.JPG/330px-NYU_student_works_on_Rube-Goldberg_part_at_Tisch_Ctr_for_Arts.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NYU_student_works_on_Rube-Goldberg_part_at_Tisch_Ctr_for_Arts.JPG/440px-NYU_student_works_on_Rube-Goldberg_part_at_Tisch_Ctr_for_Arts.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_student_works_on_Rube-Goldberg_part_at_Tisch_Ctr_for_Arts.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A student constructs a part of a 
        <a href="/wiki/Rube_Goldberg_machine" title="Rube Goldberg machine">Rube Goldberg</a> type apparatus at the Tisch Center.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>NYU operates theaters and performance facilities that are often used by the university's <a href="/wiki/Music_conservatory" title="Music conservatory" class="mw-redirect">music conservatory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tisch_School_of_the_Arts" title="Tisch School of the Arts">Tisch School of the Arts</a>. External productions are also occasionally held in NYU's facilities. The largest performance accommodations at NYU are the <a href="/wiki/Skirball_Center_for_Performing_Arts" title="Skirball Center for Performing Arts" class="mw-redirect">Skirball Center for Performing Arts</a> (850 seats) at 566 LaGuardia Place, just south of Washington Square South, and the Eisner-Lubin Auditorium (560 seats) in the Kimmel Center. Recently, the Skirball Center hosted important speeches on foreign policy by <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as the recording of the <a href="/wiki/The_Apprentice_(US_season_3)" title="The Apprentice (US season 3)" class="mw-redirect">third season finale of The Apprentice</a>. The Skirball Center is the largest performing arts facility south of <a href="/wiki/42nd_Street_(Manhattan)" title="42nd Street (Manhattan)">42nd Street</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bobst_Library">Bobst Library</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Elmer_Holmes_Bobst_Library" title="Elmer Holmes Bobst Library">Elmer Holmes Bobst Library</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NYU%27s_Bobst_library-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/NYU%27s_Bobst_library-2.jpg/170px-NYU%27s_Bobst_library-2.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/NYU%27s_Bobst_library-2.jpg/255px-NYU%27s_Bobst_library-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/NYU%27s_Bobst_library-2.jpg/340px-NYU%27s_Bobst_library-2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NYU%27s_Bobst_library-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A view of the interior of Bobst
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Elmer Holmes Bobst Library, built between 1967 and 1972, is the largest library at NYU and one of the largest academic libraries in the United States. Designed by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Johnson" title="Philip Johnson">Philip Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Foster_(architect)" title="Richard Foster (architect)">Richard Foster</a>, the 12-story, 425,000-square-foot (39,500&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) structure sits on the southern edge of Washington Square Park (at 70 Washington Square South) and is the flagship of an eight-library, 4.5 million-volume system. Bobst Library offers one Multidisciplinary Reference Center, a Research Commons, 28 miles of open-stacks shelving, and approximately 2,000 seats for student study. The library is visited by more than 6,800 users each day, and circulates more than one million books annually.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Bobst's Avery Fisher Center for Music and Media is one of the world's largest academic media centers, where students and researchers use more than 95,000 audio and video recordings per year. The Digital Studio offers a constantly evolving, leading-edge resource for faculty and student projects and promotes and supports access to digital resources for teaching, learning, research and arts events.</p> 
     <p>Bobst Library is also home to significant special collections. The Fales Collection houses one of the finest collections of English and American fiction in the United States, the unique Downtown Collection, documenting the New York literary avante-garde arts scene from the 1970s to the present, and the Food and Cookery Collection, which documents American food history with a focus on New York City. Bobst Library also houses the Tamiment Library, one of the finest collections in the world for scholarly research in labor history, socialism, anarchism, communism, and American radicalism. Tamiment includes the Robert F. Wagner Labor Archives, the Archives of Irish America, the Center for the Cold War and the U.S., and the Frederic Ewen Academic Freedom Center.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_facilities">New facilities</span></h4> 
     <p>Since the early 2000s, NYU has developed new facilities on and around its Washington Square Campus. The Kimmel Center for University Life was built in 2003 as the primary location for the university's student services offices. It also houses the Skirball Center for the Performing Arts, the Rosenthal Pavilion, the Eisner &amp; Lubin Auditorium, and the Loeb Student Center. The School of Law built Furman Hall in 2004, incorporating elements of two historic buildings into the new facade, one of which had been occupied by poet <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe">Edgar Allan Poe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2005, NYU announced the development of a new life science facility on <a href="/wiki/Waverly_Place" title="Waverly Place">Waverly Place</a>, the first new NYU science building since the opening of Meyer Hall in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2005, NYU announced plans to build a 26-floor, 190,000-square-foot (18,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) residence hall on 12th Street. The residence hall, named &quot;Founders Hall&quot;, accommodates approximately 700 undergraduates and contains a host of other student facilities. It is currently the tallest building in the <a href="/wiki/East_Village,_Manhattan" title="East Village, Manhattan">East Village</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polytechnic_Institute">Polytechnic Institute</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:First_Free_Congregational_Poly_jeh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/First_Free_Congregational_Poly_jeh.jpg/220px-First_Free_Congregational_Poly_jeh.jpg" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/First_Free_Congregational_Poly_jeh.jpg/330px-First_Free_Congregational_Poly_jeh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/First_Free_Congregational_Poly_jeh.jpg/440px-First_Free_Congregational_Poly_jeh.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:First_Free_Congregational_Poly_jeh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_Institute_of_New_York_University" title="Polytechnic Institute of New York University">NYU Poly</a> is located in New York City's borough of 
        <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_Institute_of_New_York_University" title="Polytechnic Institute of New York University">Polytechnic Institute of New York University</a>, often referred to as Polytechnic Institute of NYU, NYU Polytechnic, or NYU-Poly,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> is located in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Brooklyn" title="Downtown Brooklyn">Downtown Brooklyn</a> in the <a href="/wiki/MetroTech_Center" title="MetroTech Center">MetroTech Center</a>, the nation's largest urban university-industry <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_park" title="Science and technology park" class="mw-redirect">science and technology park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Founded in 1854, the institute adopted the <a href="/wiki/History_of_European_research_universities" title="History of European research universities">European polytechnic university model</a>, and its laboratory instruction at the undergraduate and graduate levels led to close cooperation with the industry. It is one of the oldest private technology institutes in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> and has made contributions in the fields of electrical engineering, polymer chemistry, aerospace, and microwave engineering.</p> 
     <p>NYU-Poly operates several on-campus and off-campus business incubators and is known for its success in the transfer of technology from the laboratory to the marketplace<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> according to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Economic_Development_Corporation" title="New York City Economic Development Corporation">New York City Economic Development Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-articles.economictimes.indiatimes.com-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU-Poly has state-of-the-art facilities including a brand new library and new facilities for its electrical engineering, computer science and computer engineering programs. The Brooklyn campus offers programs primarily for undergraduate students but also offers opportunities for graduate students, including executive programs for students with related experience.</p> 
     <p>NYU Poly also has campuses in downtown Manhattan, Long Island, Westchester, and in international locations such as Israel, Abu Dhabi, Shanghai, and London.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_campuses_and_facilities">Other campuses and facilities</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_School_of_Medicine" title="New York University School of Medicine">New York University School of Medicine</a> is situated near the East River waterfront at 550 First Avenue between <a href="/wiki/30th_Street_(Manhattan)" title="30th Street (Manhattan)" class="mw-redirect">East 30th</a> and <a href="/wiki/34th_Street_(Manhattan)" title="34th Street (Manhattan)">East 34th</a> Streets. The campus hosts the medical school, Tisch Hospital, and the <a href="/wiki/Rusk_Institute_of_Rehabilitation_Medicine" title="Rusk Institute of Rehabilitation Medicine">Rusk Institute of Rehabilitation Medicine</a>. Other NYU Centers across the city include NYU Hospital for Joint Diseases and the <a href="/wiki/Bellevue_Hospital_Center" title="Bellevue Hospital Center">Bellevue Hospital Center</a>. NYU's Silver School of Social Work (formerly Ehrenkranz School of Social Work) manages branch campus programs in Westchester County at <a href="/wiki/Manhattanville_College" title="Manhattanville College">Manhattanville College</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Rockland_County" title="Rockland County" class="mw-redirect">Rockland County</a> at <a href="/wiki/St._Thomas_Aquinas_College" title="St. Thomas Aquinas College">St. Thomas Aquinas College</a>, and on <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a> at the <a href="/wiki/City_University_of_New_York" title="City University of New York">City University of New York</a>'s <a href="/wiki/College_of_Staten_Island" title="College of Staten Island">College of Staten Island</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:11_W42_calendar_jeh.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/11_W42_calendar_jeh.JPG/170px-11_W42_calendar_jeh.JPG" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/11_W42_calendar_jeh.JPG/255px-11_W42_calendar_jeh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/11_W42_calendar_jeh.JPG/340px-11_W42_calendar_jeh.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:11_W42_calendar_jeh.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 11 West 42nd Street
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_Maison_francaise.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/NYU_Maison_francaise.gif/220px-NYU_Maison_francaise.gif" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/NYU_Maison_francaise.gif/330px-NYU_Maison_francaise.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/NYU_Maison_francaise.gif/440px-NYU_Maison_francaise.gif 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_Maison_francaise.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/La_Maison_Fran%C3%A7aise" title="La Maison Fran&ccedil;aise">La Maison Fran&ccedil;aise</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In <a href="/wiki/Sterling_Forest,_New_York" title="Sterling Forest, New York">Sterling Forest</a>, near Tuxedo, New York, NYU has a research facility that contains institutes, in particular the Nelson Institute of Environmental Medicine. The Midtown Center at 11 West 42nd Street and the <a href="/wiki/Woolworth_Building" title="Woolworth Building">Woolworth Building</a> in the financial district are home to NYU's continuing education programs.</p> 
     <p>NYU has two units located on the <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">Upper East Side</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_the_Study_of_the_Ancient_World" title="Institute for the Study of the Ancient World">Institute for the Study of the Ancient World</a>, a discrete entity within New York University, independent of any other school or department of the university, is located on East 84th St, while the <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_Institute_of_Fine_Arts" title="New York University Institute of Fine Arts">New York University Institute of Fine Arts</a>, a graduate school of art history and fine arts, is located at the James B. Duke Building at 1 East 78th St.</p> 
     <p>Tisch School of the Arts, Asia was NYU's first branch campus abroad. The result of a partnership between <a href="/wiki/Tisch_School_of_the_Arts" title="Tisch School of the Arts">Tisch School of the Arts</a> and the Singapore Government, it offered Master of Fine Arts degrees in animation and digital arts, dramatic writing, film and international media producing. The campus opened in fall 2007 with the intention to enroll approximately 250 students.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Anticipated enrolment figures were not achieved, financial irregularities were alleged and President Pari Sara Shirazi was dismissed from her post by NYU in November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> She subsequently announced her intention to commence legal proceedings against NYU alleging wrongful termination and defamation.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> In a letter to the Tisch Asia community dated 8 November 2012, Dean Mary Schmidt Campbell announced that the campus would close after 2014 with recruitment and admission of new students suspended with immediate effect.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the Fall of 2010, <a href="/wiki/NYU_Abu_Dhabi" title="NYU Abu Dhabi" class="mw-redirect">NYU Abu Dhabi</a> (NYUAD) opened as the University's first overseas &quot;Portal Campus&quot; with an inaugural class of 150 students.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Unlike the University's other study abroad centers, NYUAD functions as a separate liberal arts college within a University, offering complete degree programs to students admitted directly to NYUAD. NYUAD recruits students from all over the world and describes itself as the &quot;World's Honor College&quot;. The main campus for NYUAD is under construction on Saadiyat Island and is scheduled to open in 2014. Until then the school operates from a campus located in downtown Abu Dhabi.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus construction and operational costs are entirely funded by the Abu Dhabi government.<sup id="cite_ref-abu_dhabi_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abu_dhabi-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>It was announced in 2011 that NYU planned to open another portal campus, <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_Shanghai" title="New York University Shanghai">New York University Shanghai</a>, for the fall semester of 2013. It was set to have about 3,000 undergraduate students, the majority of whom would be <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a>. It was approved by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Ministry of Education of the People's Republic of China">Ministry of Education of the People's Republic of China</a> in January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU's local partner will be <a href="/wiki/East_China_Normal_University" title="East China Normal University">East China Normal University</a> (ECNU). ECNU's president <a href="/wiki/Yu_Lizhong" title="Yu Lizhong">Yu Lizhong</a> will be the chancellor and play a major role in government relations while <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_S._Lehman" title="Jeffrey S. Lehman">Jeffrey S. Lehman</a>, former president of <a href="/wiki/Cornell" title="Cornell" class="mw-redirect">Cornell</a> amongst other positions, will serve as vice chancellor and have &quot;free rein in academic affairs&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU has a host of foreign facilities used for <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" title="Study abroad" class="mw-redirect">study abroad</a> programs, referred to as Global Academic Centers. As of 2012, NYU operates 14 academic sites ? both degree-granting research university campuses and study abroad sites ? in Africa, Asia, Australia, Europe, the Middle East, and North and South America, including undergraduate academic-year and summer study abroad programs in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington_DC" title="Washington DC" class="mw-redirect">Washington DC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYU_overseas_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_overseas-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> One of the most noteworthy is the 57-acre (230,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) campus of NYU Florence <a href="/wiki/Villa_LaPietra" title="Villa LaPietra" class="mw-redirect">Villa LaPietra</a> in Italy, bequeathed by the late Sir <a href="/wiki/Harold_Acton" title="Harold Acton">Harold Acton</a> to NYU in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU also has international houses on campus, including the Deutsches Haus, <a href="/wiki/La_Maison_Fran%C3%A7aise" title="La Maison Fran&ccedil;aise">La Maison Fran&ccedil;aise</a>, <a href="/wiki/Casa_Italiana_Zerilli_Marim%C3%B2" title="Casa Italiana Zerilli Marim&ograve;">Casa Italiana Zerilli Marim&ograve;</a>, the Glucksman Ireland House, the King Juan Carlos I of Spain Center, the Hagop Kevorkian Center, an Africa House and a China House.</p> 
     <p>NYU was the founding member of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_World_Universities" title="League of World Universities">League of World Universities</a>, an <a href="/wiki/International" title="International">international</a> organization consisting of <a href="/wiki/Rector_(academia)" title="Rector (academia)">rectors</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_president" title="University president" class="mw-redirect">presidents</a> from <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban</a> <a href="/wiki/Universities" title="Universities" class="mw-redirect">universities</a> across six continents. The league and its 47 representatives gather every two years to discuss global issues in <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/L._Jay_Oliva" title="L. Jay Oliva">L. Jay Oliva</a> formed the organization in 1991 just after he was inaugurated president of New York University.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span></h3> 
     <p>New York University has made the greening of its campus a large priority. For example, NYU has been the largest university purchaser of wind energy in the U.S. since 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-NYU_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> With this switch to renewable power, NYU is achieving benefits equivalent to removing 12,000 cars from the road or planting 72,000 trees. In May 2008, the NYU Sustainability Task Force awarded $150,000 in grants to 23 projects that would focus research and efforts toward energy, food, landscape, outreach, procurement, transportation and waste.<sup id="cite_ref-At_New_York_University.2C_green_is_the_new_violet_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-At_New_York_University.2C_green_is_the_new_violet-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> These projects include a student-led bike-sharing program modeled after Paris' Velib program with 30 bikes free to students, staff, and faculty. NYU received a grade of &quot;B&quot; on the College Sustainability Report Card 2010 from the Sustainable Endowments Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU purchased 118 million <a href="/wiki/Kilowatt-hours" title="Kilowatt-hours" class="mw-redirect">kilowatt-hours</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a> during the 2006?2007 academic year ? the largest purchase of wind power by any university in the country and any institution in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenBiz.com_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenBiz.com-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> For 2007, the university expanded its purchase of wind power to 132 million kilowatt-hours.<sup id="cite_ref-NYU_buys_more_wind_power_credit_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_buys_more_wind_power_credit-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">EPA</a> ranked NYU as one of the greenest colleges in the country in its annual College &amp; University Green Power Challenge.<sup id="cite_ref-NYU_Office_of_Public_Affairs_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_Office_of_Public_Affairs-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residence_halls">Residence halls</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_residence_halls" title="New York University residence halls">New York University residence halls</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Square_Village.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Washington_Square_Village.jpg/220px-Washington_Square_Village.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Washington_Square_Village.jpg/330px-Washington_Square_Village.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Washington_Square_Village.jpg/440px-Washington_Square_Village.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Square_Village.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_Village" title="Washington Square Village">Washington Square Village</a>, home to NYU faculty and graduate students
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>With approximately 12,500 residents, NYU has the seventh-largest university housing system in the U.S. as of 2007, and one of the largest among private schools.<sup id="cite_ref-housingranking_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-housingranking-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU's undergraduate housing system consists of 21 buildings. Uniquely, many of NYU's residence halls are converted <a href="/wiki/Apartment" title="Apartment">apartment</a> complexes or old hotels. In general, NYU residence halls receive favorable ratings, and some are opulent. Many rooms are spacious and contain amenities considered rare for individual college residence hall rooms, such as kitchens, lavatories, living rooms and common areas.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The university operates its own transit system to transport its students by <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">bus</a> to its campus.</p> 
     <p>Undergraduate students are guaranteed housing during their enrollment at NYU. Most freshman residence halls are located near the Washington Square area. While nearly all of the residence halls that primarily house sophomores are located near the <a href="/wiki/Union_Square_(New_York_City)" title="Union Square (New York City)">Union Square</a> area, two former residence halls were located in the <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Manhattan" title="Financial District, Manhattan">Financial District</a> and one is still in use in <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">Chinatown</a>. All of NYU's residence halls are governed by the <a href="/wiki/Residence_hall_association" title="Residence hall association">Inter-Residence Hall Council</a> (IRHC), an umbrella student council organization.</p> 
     <p>In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_College_and_University_Residence_Halls" title="National Association of College and University Residence Halls">National Association of College and University Residence Halls</a> named NYU the National School of the Year for IRHC and <a href="/wiki/NRHH" title="NRHH" class="mw-redirect">NRHH</a>'s strong efforts over the past year. In addition, NYU was named the National Program of the Year for UltraViolet Live, the annual inter-hall competition that raises funds for <a href="/wiki/Relay_For_Life" title="Relay For Life">Relay For Life</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools_and_colleges">Schools and colleges</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NYU-Gallatin_School.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/NYU-Gallatin_School.jpg/170px-NYU-Gallatin_School.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/NYU-Gallatin_School.jpg/255px-NYU-Gallatin_School.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/NYU-Gallatin_School.jpg/340px-NYU-Gallatin_School.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NYU-Gallatin_School.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Flags identify NYU buildings in the city. This flag is for the 
        <a href="/wiki/Gallatin_School_of_Individualized_Study" title="Gallatin School of Individualized Study">Gallatin School of Individualized Study</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>New York University comprises 18 colleges, schools, and institutes.<sup id="cite_ref-schools_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schools-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Arts &amp; Science</li> 
     </ul> 
     <dl> 
      <dd> 
       <ul> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/NYU_College_of_Arts_and_Science" title="NYU College of Arts and Science" class="mw-redirect">College of Arts and Science</a> (CAS)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/NYU_College_of_Arts_and_Science#Liberal_Studies" title="NYU College of Arts and Science" class="mw-redirect">Liberal Studies</a> (LSP)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/NYU_Graduate_School_of_Arts_and_Science" title="NYU Graduate School of Arts and Science" class="mw-redirect">Graduate School of Arts and Science</a> (GSAS)</li> 
       </ul> 
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/NYU_College_of_Dentistry" title="NYU College of Dentistry" class="mw-redirect">College of Dentistry</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/New_York_University_College_of_Nursing" title="New York University College of Nursing">College of Nursing</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Courant_Institute_of_Mathematical_Sciences" title="Courant Institute of Mathematical Sciences">Courant Institute of Mathematical Sciences</a> (Courant)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Gallatin_School_of_Individualized_Study" title="Gallatin School of Individualized Study">Gallatin School of Individualized Study</a> (Gallatin)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/NYU_Institute_of_Fine_Arts" title="NYU Institute of Fine Arts" class="mw-redirect">Institute of Fine Arts</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Institute_for_the_Study_of_the_Ancient_World" title="Institute for the Study of the Ancient World">Institute for the Study of the Ancient World</a> (ISAW)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Leonard_N._Stern_School_of_Business" title="Leonard N. Stern School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Leonard N. Stern School of Business</a> (Stern)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/New_York_University_Abu_Dhabi" title="New York University Abu Dhabi">New York University Abu Dhabi</a> (NYUAD)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_Institute_of_New_York_University" title="Polytechnic Institute of New York University">Polytechnic Institute</a> (Poly)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Wagner_Graduate_School_of_Public_Service" title="Robert F. Wagner Graduate School of Public Service">Robert F. Wagner Graduate School of Public Service</a> (Wagner)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Continuing_and_Professional_Studies" title="NYU School of Continuing and Professional Studies" class="mw-redirect">School of Continuing and Professional Studies</a> (SCPS)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Law" title="NYU School of Law" class="mw-redirect">School of Law</a> (Law)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Medicine" title="NYU School of Medicine" class="mw-redirect">School of Medicine</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Social_Work" title="NYU School of Social Work" class="mw-redirect">Silver School of Social Work</a> (Silver)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Steinhardt_School_of_Culture,_Education,_and_Human_Development" title="Steinhardt School of Culture, Education, and Human Development">Steinhardt School of Culture, Education, and Human Development</a> (Steinhardt)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Tisch_School_of_the_Arts" title="Tisch School of the Arts">Tisch School of the Arts</a> (Tisch)</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Arts and Science is currently the largest academic unit of the university. It has three subdivisions, which include the <a href="/wiki/NYU_College_of_Arts_and_Science" title="NYU College of Arts and Science" class="mw-redirect">College of Arts and Science</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NYU_Graduate_School_of_Arts_and_Science" title="NYU Graduate School of Arts and Science" class="mw-redirect">Graduate School of Arts and Science</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NYU_College_of_Arts_and_Science#Liberal_Studies" title="NYU College of Arts and Science" class="mw-redirect">Liberal Studies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The College of Arts and Science (CAS) was the only school when NYU was founded.</p> 
     <p>Other undergraduate schools include the <a href="/wiki/Gallatin_School_of_Individualized_Study" title="Gallatin School of Individualized Study">Gallatin School of Individualized Study</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Social_Work" title="NYU School of Social Work" class="mw-redirect">School of Social Work</a>, the Preston Robert Tisch Center for Hospitality, Tourism and Sports Management at the <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_School_of_Continuing_and_Professional_Studies" title="New York University School of Continuing and Professional Studies">New York University School of Continuing and Professional Studies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Steinhardt_School_of_Culture,_Education_and_Human_Development" title="Steinhardt School of Culture, Education and Human Development" class="mw-redirect">Steinhardt School of Culture, Education and Human Development</a> (the first school of education in the United States), the <a href="/wiki/Stern_School_of_Business" title="Stern School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Stern School of Business</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tisch_School_of_the_Arts" title="Tisch School of the Arts">Tisch School of the Arts</a>. In 2008, Polytechnic University merged with NYU to become the <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_Institute_of_New_York_University" title="Polytechnic Institute of New York University">Polytechnic Institute</a>, providing NYU with an engineering school for the first time in three decades.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also plans to open up the Liberal Studies Program to all students for the Fall 2012 term by process of application, rather than by referral (as it has been since 1972).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several schools at NYU also offer graduate and professional programs. NYU's postgraduate schools and divisions include the <a href="/wiki/Gallatin_School_of_Individualized_Study" title="Gallatin School of Individualized Study">Gallatin School of Individualized Study</a>, <a href="/wiki/NYU_College_of_Dentistry" title="NYU College of Dentistry" class="mw-redirect">College of Dentistry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_College_of_Nursing" title="New York University College of Nursing">College of Nursing</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Courant_Institute_of_Mathematical_Sciences" title="Courant Institute of Mathematical Sciences">Courant Institute of Mathematical Sciences</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NYU_Institute_of_Fine_Arts" title="NYU Institute of Fine Arts" class="mw-redirect">Institute of Fine Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_the_Study_of_the_Ancient_World" title="Institute for the Study of the Ancient World">Institute for the Study of the Ancient World</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_Institute_of_New_York_University" title="Polytechnic Institute of New York University">Polytechnic Institute</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Continuing_and_Professional_Studies" title="NYU School of Continuing and Professional Studies" class="mw-redirect">School of Continuing and Professional Studies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Law" title="NYU School of Law" class="mw-redirect">School of Law</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Medicine" title="NYU School of Medicine" class="mw-redirect">School of Medicine</a>, the Graduate School of Arts and Science, and the <a href="/wiki/Wagner_Graduate_School_of_Public_Service" title="Wagner Graduate School of Public Service" class="mw-redirect">Wagner Graduate School of Public Service</a>.</p> 
     <p>NYU closed its School of Aeronautics in 1973, its College of Veterinary Surgeons in 1922, and has merged various programs with other schools. For example, its School of Engineering merged with the Polytechnic University of New York in 1973, and NYU's former College Hofstra Memorial became <a href="/wiki/Hofstra_University" title="Hofstra University">independent</a> in 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
