     <p>NYU is ranked 22nd among all universities in the world by Global University Ranking (maintained by <a href="/wiki/Wuhan_University" title="Wuhan University">Wuhan University</a>), and 20th nationally and 27th globally by the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (formerly maintained by <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiaotong_University" title="Shanghai Jiaotong University" class="mw-redirect">Shanghai Jiaotong University</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-globaluniversitiesranking.org_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globaluniversitiesranking.org-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arwu.org_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arwu.org-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU's schools and institutes are regularly ranked within the top 10 worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-ranking-pg-phil_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ranking-pg-phil-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NewStandard_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewStandard-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kalaitzidakis_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaitzidakis-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_NYU_Wagner_Education_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_NYU_Wagner_Education-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TBOTB_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TBOTB-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GradSchoolsAppliedMath_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradSchoolsAppliedMath-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_Undergrad_Business_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_Undergrad_Business-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ranking-us-law_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ranking-us-law-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU's <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a> department is ranked #1 among 50 philosophy departments in the English-speaking world.<sup id="cite_ref-ranking-pg-phil_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ranking-pg-phil-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU is also ranked #1 in <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, Italian, and <a href="/wiki/Theater" title="Theater" class="mw-redirect">theater</a> in the U.S. by the Faculty Scholarly Productivity Index, which uses data, such as faculty publications, grants, and honors and awards to rank 104 doctoral programs in 10 academic disciplines based on the research productivity of faculty members.<sup id="cite_ref-NewStandard_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewStandard-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Courant_Institute_of_Mathematical_Sciences" title="Courant Institute of Mathematical Sciences">Courant Institute of Mathematical Sciences</a> is ranked #1 in applied mathematics in the U.S.,<sup id="cite_ref-GradSchoolsAppliedMath_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradSchoolsAppliedMath-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> #5 in citation impact worldwide and #12 in citations worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-MathRankedScienceWatch_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MathRankedScienceWatch-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> The Academic Ranking of World Universities ranked NYU's math department #14 overall among top universities globally.<sup id="cite_ref-arwu-math_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arwu-math-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The Courant Institute of Mathematical Sciences is also known for its research in pure mathematical areas, such as <a href="/wiki/Partial_differential_equations" title="Partial differential equations" class="mw-redirect">partial differential equations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Probability" title="Probability">probability</a> and <a href="/wiki/Differential_geometry" title="Differential geometry">differential geometry</a> (Professors <a href="/wiki/Peter_Lax" title="Peter Lax">Peter Lax</a>, <a href="/wiki/S._R._Srinivasa_Varadhan" title="S. R. Srinivasa Varadhan">S. R. Srinivasa Varadhan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gromov_(mathematician)" title="Mikhail Gromov (mathematician)" class="mw-redirect">Mikhail Gromov</a> won the 2005, 2007 and 2009 <a href="/wiki/Abel_Prize" title="Abel Prize">Abel Prize</a> respectively for their research in these areas) as well as applied mathematical areas, such as <a href="/wiki/Computational_biology" title="Computational biology">computational biology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computational_neuroscience" title="Computational neuroscience">computational neuroscience</a>.</p> 
     <p>NYU's <a href="/wiki/Stern_School_of_Business" title="Stern School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Stern School of Business</a> undergraduate program is ranked #5 by <i><a href="/wiki/US_News" title="US News" class="mw-redirect">US News</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_Undergrad_Business_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_Undergrad_Business-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> and #12 by <i><a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect">BusinessWeek</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> (ranked #8 in 2009). Stern's MBA program is ranked #10 in <i>US News</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-GradSchoolsMBA_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GradSchoolsMBA-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> #11 in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Best_Full-time_MBA_Programmes_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Best_Full-time_MBA_Programmes-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> #15 in the <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> #16 in <i>BusinessWeek</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> and #2 by research contribution.<sup id="cite_ref-citm.utdallas.edu_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citm.utdallas.edu-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU's <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a> department is regularly ranked among the top 10 worldwide, including #6 in an updated Dusansky-Vernon <i><a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Economic_Literature" title="Journal of Economic Literature">Journal of Economic Literature</a></i> study, which ranked departments in terms of the publications of their faculty in top-five rated journals.<sup id="cite_ref-Kalaitzidakis_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalaitzidakis-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_of_U.S._Economics_Departments_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_of_U.S._Economics_Departments-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU was ranked #9 globally in economics/business by the Academic Ranking of World Universities in 2009, one ahead of <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-arwu-econ_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arwu-econ-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Law" title="NYU School of Law" class="mw-redirect">School of Law</a> is ranked #6 among <a href="/wiki/Law_school" title="Law school">law schools</a> in the U.S. by <i>US News and World Report</i> (and has been ranked by the same source as high as #4 in previous years).<sup id="cite_ref-ranking-us-law_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ranking-us-law-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> The law school is particularly noted as the nation's top law school in tax law, international law, and <a href="/wiki/Jurisprudence" title="Jurisprudence">jurisprudence</a> (philosophy of law).<sup id="cite_ref-Law_Specialty_Rankings:_Tax_Law_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_Specialty_Rankings:_Tax_Law-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USNews_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNews-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brian_Leiter_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brian_Leiter-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of NYU's alumni have been appointed justices of the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Medicine" title="NYU School of Medicine" class="mw-redirect">NYU School of Medicine</a> is ranked #26, and #11 for best AIDS program, by <i>US News and World Report</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> The School of Medicine's alumni include four <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> recipients.</p> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" title="Princeton Review" class="mw-redirect">Princeton Review</a></i> ranks <a href="/wiki/NYU-Poly" title="NYU-Poly" class="mw-redirect">NYU-Poly</a>'s undergraduate electrical engineering program #12 in the nation, and its graduate electrical engineering program #13 in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Consus_Group_LLC_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Consus_Group_LLC-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Forbes.com" title="Forbes.com" class="mw-redirect">Forbes.com</a> regularly ranks NYU-Poly among the top 10 in its list of ?Top Colleges for Getting Rich?.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, NYU-Poly was ranked #21 by graduate engineering enrollment in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> according to the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_for_Engineering_Education" title="American Society for Engineering Education">American Society for Engineering Education</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> and #34 on &quot;The World's Best Engineering Schools&quot; list by <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-businessinsider.com_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businessinsider.com-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Social_sciences" title="Social sciences" class="mw-redirect">social sciences</a>, NYU was ranked #10 by the Academic Ranking of World Universities in 2009, and #11 among Shanghai Jiao Tong University's world's top 100 universities.<sup id="cite_ref-arwu-social_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arwu-social-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ranking-sjt-social_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ranking-sjt-social-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU's <a href="/wiki/Steinhardt_School_of_Culture,_Education_and_Human_Development" title="Steinhardt School of Culture, Education and Human Development" class="mw-redirect">Steinhardt School of Culture, Education and Human Development</a> has one of the top 15 education programs in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU's <a href="/wiki/Wagner_Graduate_School_of_Public_Service" title="Wagner Graduate School of Public Service" class="mw-redirect">Wagner Graduate School of Public Service</a> is ranked 6th nationally by <i>US News and World Report</i>. In addition, several of Wagner's public affairs specializations are ranked in the top 10.<sup id="cite_ref-The_NYU_Wagner_Education_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_NYU_Wagner_Education-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU's <a href="/wiki/Tisch_School_of_the_Arts" title="Tisch School of the Arts">Tisch School of the Arts</a> has produced more Academy Award winners than any other film institution in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-academyawards_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academyawards-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU Tisch members are regularly nominated to win Oscars, Emmys, and other awards: in 2011, 15 Tisch members were nominated for Oscars, and 10 Tisch members claimed Emmys.<sup id="cite_ref-NYU_Oscars_2011_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_Oscars_2011-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYU_Emmys_2011_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_Emmys_2011-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU's <a href="/wiki/Creative_Writing" title="Creative Writing" class="mw-redirect">Creative Writing</a> Program (GSAS) was included within <i><a href="/wiki/The_Atlantic" title="The Atlantic">The Atlantic</a>'s</i> list of &quot;Top Ten Graduate Programs in Creative Writing&quot;, having been selected from a pool of over 250 such programs currently active in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-TBOTB_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TBOTB-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>From 2004 to 2007, NYU was ranked by the <i>Princeton Review</i> as America's #1 &quot;dream school&quot; among high school seniors.<sup id="cite_ref-dreamschool_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dreamschool-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008 however, NYU slipped to 4th place in the <i>Princeton Review</i> poll, led only by Harvard, Yale, and Stanford, citing better financial aid among Ivy Leagues and using additional parental ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, NYU was named by <a href="/wiki/Kaplan,_Inc." title="Kaplan, Inc.">Kaplan</a> as one of the &quot;New Ivies&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU ranks 30th on the <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a>, which ranks the world's universities based on a composite indicator that takes into account both the volume of the Web contents (number of web pages and files) and the visibility and impact of these web publications according to the number of external inlinks (site citations) they received.</p> 
     <p>NYU ranks #1 among &quot;Universities That Turn Research Into Revenue&quot; according to <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> According to data compiled by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes_Magazine" title="Forbes Magazine" class="mw-redirect">Forbes Magazine</a></i> in 2008, NYU ranks 7th among universities that have produced the largest number of living billionaires.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions_and_enrollment">Admissions and enrollment</span></h3> 
     <p>NYU has a large, diverse student population representing all 50 states and more than 130 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-NYU_fast_facts_2012_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_fast_facts_2012-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> About 25?30% of NYU's incoming freshmen are from New York, New Jersey, and Connecticut, while the remaining 70?75% are from outside the <a href="/wiki/Tri-State_Region" title="Tri-State Region" class="mw-redirect">Tri-State area</a>. 10% of the students are from one of New York City's <a href="/wiki/The_five_boroughs" title="The five boroughs" class="mw-redirect">five boroughs</a>. NYU's main <a href="/wiki/Feeder_schools" title="Feeder schools" class="mw-redirect">feeder schools</a> reflect a heavy Northeastern U.S. presence, and particularly a strong New York City influence. Among NYU's top feeder schools are prestigious high schools including <a href="/wiki/Stuyvesant_High_School" title="Stuyvesant High School">Stuyvesant High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Technical_High_School" title="Brooklyn Technical High School">Brooklyn Technical High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bronx_High_School_of_Science" title="Bronx High School of Science" class="mw-redirect">Bronx High School of Science</a>, and several top private schools in the northeast.</p> 
     <p>Out of the 42,242 applicants for the undergraduate class of 2015, around 30% were offered admission (when including admission statistics for the Liberal Studies Program). Out of the acceptances, 38% consisted of <a href="/wiki/Early_decision" title="Early decision">early decision</a> applicants, who together form 23% of the undergraduate class. 4,650 freshmen joined NYU in Fall 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-nyu_facts_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyu_facts-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, NYU achieved a record low admission rate of 24% of applicants.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The middle 50% of <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> scores for the class of 2015 was 630?730 for critical reading, 650?750 for math, and 660?750 for writing. The middle 50% of <a href="/wiki/ACT_(test)" title="ACT (test)">ACT</a> scores for the class of 2015 was between 29 and 31. The average GPA corresponds with an A-range letter grade, and most incoming students were in the top 10% of their class.<sup id="cite_ref-nyu_facts_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyu_facts-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On June 21, 2010, NYU announced the profile of the first freshman class of <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_Abu_Dhabi" title="New York University Abu Dhabi">NYU Abu Dhabi (NYUAD)</a>, which calls itself the &quot;World's Honors College&quot;. The class includes 150 students, 36% of whom are from the United States. The average SAT score was 1470 and the acceptance rate was 2.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In a quest to find talented individuals from around the world and become a truly global university, New York University signed an agreement to accept high-performing students from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_People" title="University of the People">University of the People</a> who are eligible to apply to New York University's Abu Dhabi campus. The Abu Dhabi campus is able to grant generous financial aid, enabling those students who are eligible, albeit disadvantaged financially, to attend the highly selective NYU Abu Dhabi campus.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>During the admissions process, some institutions at NYU are relatively more selective than others in certain categories, depending on the institution's educational goals. For example, NYU's Abu Dhabi program focuses more than other schools at NYU on students who have demonstrated a history of leadership, whereas NYU's Tisch School of the Arts focuses more on artistic and creative traits than do other schools at NYU.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NYU is among the top 15 universities in the U.S. in the number of <a href="/wiki/National_Merit_Scholar" title="National Merit Scholar" class="mw-redirect">National Merit Scholars</a> in the first-year undergraduate student body.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget_and_fundraising">Budget and fundraising</span></h2> 
     <p>New York University has successfully completed a seven-year, $2.5 billion campaign, surpassing expectations by raising more than $3 billion over the seven-year period.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Started in 2001, this campaign was the university's largest in its history, in which they planned to &quot;raise $1 million per day for <a href="/wiki/Scholarships" title="Scholarships" class="mw-redirect">scholarships</a> and <a href="/wiki/Financial_aid_(educational_expenses)" title="Financial aid (educational expenses)" class="mw-redirect">financial aid</a>, faculty building, new academic initiatives, and enhancing NYU's physical facilities&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-campaignnews_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campaignnews-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The campaign included a $50 million gift from the Tisch family (after which one building and the <a href="/wiki/Tisch_School_of_the_Arts" title="Tisch School of the Arts">art school</a> are named) and a $60 million gift from six <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustees</a> called &quot;The Partners Fund&quot;, aimed at hiring new faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-campaignnews_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campaignnews-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-campaign_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-campaign-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 15, 2007 the university announced that the Silver family donated $50 million to the <a href="/wiki/NYU_School_of_Social_Work" title="NYU School of Social Work" class="mw-redirect">School of Social Work</a>, which will be renamed as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> This is the largest donation ever to a school of social work in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The 2007?2008 academic year was the most successful fundraising year to date for NYU, with the school raising $698 million in only the first 11 months of the year, representing a 70% increase in donations from the prior year.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> The University also recently announced plans for NYU's Call to Action, a new initiative to ask alumni and donors to support financial aid for students at NYU.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has announced a 25-year strategic development plan, scheduled to coincide with its <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/bicentennial" class="extiw" title="wikt:bicentennial">bicentennial</a> in 2031. Included in the &quot;NYU 200&quot; plans are increasing resident and academic space, hiring additional exemplary faculty, and involving the New York City community in a transparent planning process. Additionally, NYU hopes to make their buildings more environmentally friendly, which will be facilitated by an evaluation of all campus spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> As a part of this plan, NYU purchased 118 million <a href="/wiki/Kilowatt-hours" title="Kilowatt-hours" class="mw-redirect">kilowatt-hours</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a> during the 2006?2007 academic year ? the largest purchase of wind power by any university in the country and any institution in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenBiz.com_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenBiz.com-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> For 2007, the university expanded its purchase of wind power to 132 million kilowatt-hours.<sup id="cite_ref-NYU_buys_more_wind_power_credit_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_buys_more_wind_power_credit-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">EPA</a> ranked NYU as one of the greenest colleges in the country in its annual College &amp; University Green Power Challenge.<sup id="cite_ref-NYU_Office_of_Public_Affairs_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYU_Office_of_Public_Affairs-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Student_Senators_Council" title="Student Senators Council" class="mw-redirect">Student Senators Council</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">governing student body</a> at NYU. The SSC has been involved in controversial debates on campus, including a campuswide ban on the sale of <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Company" title="Coca-Cola Company" class="mw-redirect">Coca-Cola products</a> in 2005, and the <a href="/wiki/Graduate_Student_Organizing_Committee" title="Graduate Student Organizing Committee">Graduate Student Organizing Committee</a> unionization in 2001 and subsequent strike in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> This ban was lifted by the University Senate on February 5, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_Program_Board_Logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/59/NYU_Program_Board_Logo.png" width="200" height="131" class="thumbimage" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_Program_Board_Logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> NYU Program Board logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_Thomas_SLF235_30620_on_Shuttle_Route_A.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NYU_Thomas_SLF235_30620_on_Shuttle_Route_A.jpg/220px-NYU_Thomas_SLF235_30620_on_Shuttle_Route_A.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NYU_Thomas_SLF235_30620_on_Shuttle_Route_A.jpg/330px-NYU_Thomas_SLF235_30620_on_Shuttle_Route_A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NYU_Thomas_SLF235_30620_on_Shuttle_Route_A.jpg/440px-NYU_Thomas_SLF235_30620_on_Shuttle_Route_A.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_Thomas_SLF235_30620_on_Shuttle_Route_A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A bus system transports students to and from the far ends of campus.
       </div>

     </div> 
     <p>NYU has over 450 student clubs and organizations on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to the sports teams, fraternities, sororities, and study clubs, there are many organizations on campus that focus on entertainment, arts, and culture. These organizations include various <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student media</a> clubs: for instance, the daily <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a> the <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_News" title="Washington Square News">Washington Square News</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/NYU_Local" title="NYU Local">NYU Local</a> daily blog, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Plague_(magazine)" title="The Plague (magazine)">The Plague</a></i> comedy magazine, and the literary journals <i>Washington Square Review</i> and <i>The Minetta Review</i>, as well as student-run event producers such as the NYU Program Board and the Inter-Residence Hall Council. It also operates <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station" class="mw-redirect">radio station</a> <a href="/wiki/WNYU-FM" title="WNYU-FM">WNYU-FM</a> 89.1 with a diverse <a href="/wiki/College_radio" title="College radio" class="mw-redirect">college radio</a> format, transmitting to the entire <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York metropolitan area</a> from the original campus, and via booster station WNYU-FM1 which fills in the signal in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">lower Manhattan</a> from atop one of the Silver Towers, next to the <a href="/wiki/American_football_field" title="American football field" class="mw-redirect">football field</a> at the Washington Square campus.</p> 
     <p>During the University Heights era, an apparent rift evolved with some organizations distancing themselves from students from the downtown schools. The exclusive <a href="/wiki/Philomathean_Society_at_New_York_University" title="Philomathean Society at New York University" class="mw-redirect">Philomathean Society</a> operated from 1832 to 1888 (formally giving way in 1907 and reconstituted into the Andiron Club). Included among the Andiron's regulations was &quot;Rule No.11: Have no relations save the most casual and informal kind with the downtown schools&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Eucleian_Society" title="The Eucleian Society" class="mw-redirect">The Eucleian Society</a>, rival to the Philomathean Society, was founded in 1832. The Knights of the Lamp was a social organization founded in 1914 at the School of Commerce. This organization met every full moon and had a glowworm as its mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Red_Dragon_Society" title="Red Dragon Society">Red Dragon Society</a>, founded in 1898, is thought to be the most selective society at NYU. In addition, NYU's first <a href="/wiki/Yearbook" title="Yearbook">yearbook</a> was formed by fraternities and &quot;secret societies&quot; at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>New York University has traditions which have persisted across campuses. Since the beginning of the 20th century initiation ceremonies have welcomed incoming NYU freshmen. At the Bronx University Heights Campus, seniors used to grab unsuspecting freshmen, take them to a horse-watering trough, and then dunk them head-first into what was known colloquially as &quot;the Fountain of Knowledge&quot;. This underground initiation took place until the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Today freshmen take part in university-sponsored activities during what is called &quot;Welcome Week&quot;. In addition, throughout the year the university traditionally holds Apple Fest (an apple-themed country fest that began at the University Heights campus), the Violet Ball (a dance in the atrium of Bobst Library), Strawberry Fest (featuring New York City's longest <a href="/wiki/Shortcake" title="Shortcake">Strawberry Shortcake</a>), and the semi-annual <a href="/wiki/Midnight_breakfast" title="Midnight breakfast">midnight breakfast</a> where Student Affairs administrators serve free breakfast to students before <a href="/wiki/Final_examination" title="Final examination">finals</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span></h3> 
     <p>Some of the first <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities</a> in the country were formed at NYU.<sup id="cite_ref-psiupsilon_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psiupsilon-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alphaepsilonpi_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alphaepsilonpi-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_Sororities" title="Fraternities and Sororities" class="mw-redirect">Greek life</a> first formed on the NYU campus in 1837 when <a href="/wiki/Psi_Upsilon" title="Psi Upsilon">Psi Upsilon</a> chartered its Delta Chapter.<sup id="cite_ref-psiupsilon_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psiupsilon-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> The first fraternities at NYU were social ones. With their athletic, professional, intellectual, and service activities, later groups sought to attract students who also formed other groups. Since then, Greek letter organizations have proliferated to include 25 social fraternities and sororities. Approximately 7% of NYU students choose to join fraternities or sororities.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Four governing boards oversee Greek life at the university. The Interfraternity Council (IFC) has jurisdiction over all twelve recognized fraternities on campus. Eight sororities are under the jurisdiction of the Panhellenic Council (PhC), which features six national sororities (???, ???, ???, ???, KK? and ZT?) and two local sororities (A?? and ???). Five multicultural organizations maintain membership in the Multicultural Greek Council (MGC), including two fraternities and three sororities. All three of the aforementioned boards are managed under the auspices of the Inter-Greek Council.</p> 
     <p>Greek organizations have historical significance at NYU. <a href="/wiki/Delta_Phi_Epsilon_(social)" title="Delta Phi Epsilon (social)">Delta Phi Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Psi" title="Zeta Psi">Zeta Psi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tau_Delta_Phi" title="Tau Delta Phi">Tau Delta Phi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Psi" title="Alpha Kappa Psi">Alpha Kappa Psi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delta_Sigma_Pi" title="Delta Sigma Pi">Delta Sigma Pi</a> were founded at NYU. <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Psi" title="Zeta Psi">Zeta Psi Fraternity of North America</a> was chartered in 1847,<sup id="cite_ref-alphaepsilonpi_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alphaepsilonpi-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delta_Sigma_Pi" title="Delta Sigma Pi">Delta Sigma Pi</a> in 1907,<sup id="cite_ref-deltsigmapi_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deltsigmapi-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a> in 1913.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> Delta Phi Epsilon was founded in 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> The NYU Gamma chapter of <a href="/wiki/Delta_Phi" title="Delta Phi">Delta Phi</a>, founded in 1841, is the longest continuously active fraternity chapter in the world, having never gone inactive since its establishment. Delta Phi is also the oldest continuously active fraternity in the United States, being the only organization in the original Union Triad to remain active since its institute. The NYU Gamma chapter of <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Beta_Tau" title="Zeta Beta Tau">Zeta Beta Tau</a> is the oldest active ZBT chapter in the country.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/NYU_Violets" title="NYU Violets">NYU Violets</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NYUAthleticsLogo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/NYUAthleticsLogo.jpg/220px-NYUAthleticsLogo.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/NYUAthleticsLogo.jpg/330px-NYUAthleticsLogo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/NYUAthleticsLogo.jpg/440px-NYUAthleticsLogo.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NYUAthleticsLogo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> NYU Athletics Logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>NYU's sports teams are referred to as the <a href="/wiki/NYU_Violets" title="NYU Violets">NYU Violets</a>, the colors being the trademarked hue &quot;NYU Violet&quot;, and white. Since 1981, the school <a href="/wiki/Mascot" title="Mascot">mascot</a> has been a bobcat, whose origin can be traced back to the abbreviation then being used by the Bobst Library computerized catalog ? short: Bobcat.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> NYU's sports teams include men's and women's varsity basketball, cross country, fencing, golf, soccer, swimming and diving, tennis, track and field, volleyball, and wrestling.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> All of NYU's sports teams participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA's</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division III</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_Athletic_Association" title="University Athletic Association">University Athletic Association</a>, with the exceptions of Men's Volleyball, which competes in the Division I Eastern Collegiate Volleyball Association, and fencing, which also participates in Division I. The <a href="/wiki/National_Intercollegiate_Women%27s_Fencing_Association" title="National Intercollegiate Women's Fencing Association">National Intercollegiate Women's Fencing Association</a> (NIWFA) was founded by NYU freshmen <a href="/wiki/Julia_Jones_Pugliese" title="Julia Jones Pugliese">Julia Jones</a> and Dorothy Hafner.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_Hockey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/NYU_Hockey.jpg/220px-NYU_Hockey.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/NYU_Hockey.jpg/330px-NYU_Hockey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/NYU_Hockey.jpg/440px-NYU_Hockey.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_Hockey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> An NYU Men's Hockey player
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>While NYU has had <a href="/wiki/All-American" title="All-American" class="mw-redirect">All-American</a> football players, the school has not had a varsity <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> team since 1952. Notable football players include Hall of Fame <a href="/wiki/Ken_Strong" title="Ken Strong">Ken Strong</a> (1956) and <a href="/wiki/Ed_Smith_(football_player)" title="Ed Smith (football player)" class="mw-redirect">Ed Smith</a> (1934), the model for the <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 1940 season, before a football game between NYU and <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Tigers" title="Missouri Tigers">Missouri</a>, students protested against the &quot;gentlemen's agreement&quot; to exclude <a href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American" class="mw-redirect">black</a> athletes (at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Missouri" title="University of Missouri">Missouri's</a> request). The protest against this practice is the first time such protests were recorded to have occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_volleyball.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/NYU_volleyball.jpg/170px-NYU_volleyball.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/NYU_volleyball.jpg/255px-NYU_volleyball.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/NYU_volleyball.jpg/340px-NYU_volleyball.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NYU_volleyball.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Men's Volleyball in 
        <a href="/wiki/Coles_Sports_and_Recreation_Center" title="Coles Sports and Recreation Center">Coles Sports Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>NYU, within its brief history in NCAA Division III, has won two national team championships and many league championships. In 1997, the Women's Basketball team, led by head coach Janice Quinn, won a national championship over the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Eau_Claire" title="University of Wisconsin?Eau Claire">University of Wisconsin?Eau Claire</a> and in 2007 returned to the Final Four. NYU Men's Basketball and head coach <a href="/wiki/Joe_Nesci" title="Joe Nesci">Joe Nesci</a> appeared in the Division III National Championship game in 1994. In 2006, the Men's Cross Country team finished 2nd at the NCAA Championship. The following year, behind the emotional support of Dan Schwartzman, the Men's Cross Country team won the 2007 NCAA National Cross Country Championship at St. Olaf College in Minnesota.</p> 
     <p>NYU Men's and Women's Swimming teams captured consecutive (2004?2005) <a href="/wiki/Eastern_College_Athletic_Conference" title="Eastern College Athletic Conference">Eastern College Athletic Conference</a> (ECAC) Division III Swimming and Diving Championships. Christian Majdick of the Men's Track and Field team captured the NCAA Division III championship for the triple jump in 2003. Lauren Henkel, a track and field athlete and the current assistant coach of the Women's Track and Field team, acquired <a href="/wiki/All-American" title="All-American" class="mw-redirect">All-American</a> status three times for High Jump. The Men's Soccer team won its league ECAC championship in the 2005?2006 season.</p> 
     <p>The Men's Ice Hockey team participates in the ACHA (DII) and is in the SECHL. During the 2003?2004 season, the Ice Hockey team finished second (2nd) in the nation, losing to <a href="/wiki/Oakland_University" title="Oakland University">Oakland University</a> of Michigan.</p> 
     <p>NYU students also compete in club and intramural sports, including <a href="/wiki/Badminton" title="Badminton">badminton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">crew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squash_(sport)" title="Squash (sport)">squash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martial_arts" title="Martial arts">martial arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Triathlon" title="Triathlon">triathlon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_(sport)" title="Ultimate (sport)">ultimate</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Coles_Sports_and_Recreation_Center" title="Coles Sports and Recreation Center">Coles Sports and Recreation Center</a> serves as the home base of several of NYU's intercollegiate athletic teams. Many of NYU's varsity teams play their games at various facilities and fields throughout Manhattan because of the scarcity of space for playing fields near campus. In 2002, NYU opened the <a href="/wiki/Palladium_(New_York_City)" title="Palladium (New York City)">Palladium</a> Athletic Facility as the second on-campus recreational facility. In the same year, NYU's intramural dance team won the National Championship title at the National Dance Alliance (NDA) Division III competition in Daytona, Florida.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_and_alumni">Faculty and alumni</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_University_alumni" title="List of New York University alumni">List of New York University alumni</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_University_faculty_and_staff" title="List of New York University faculty and staff">List of New York University faculty and staff</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_NYU_Polytechnic_Institute_people" title="List of NYU Polytechnic Institute people">List of NYU Polytechnic Institute people</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_NYU_Stern_people" title="List of NYU Stern people">List of NYU Stern people</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_NYU_Law_School_people" title="List of NYU Law School people">List of NYU Law School people</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_NYU_Tisch_School_of_the_Arts_people" title="List of NYU Tisch School of the Arts people">List of NYU Tisch School of the Arts people</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_NYU_Courant_Institute_people" title="List of NYU Courant Institute people">List of NYU Courant Institute people</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_NYU_GSAS_people" title="List of NYU GSAS people">List of NYU GSAS people</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_NYU_CAS_people" title="List of NYU CAS people" class="mw-redirect">List of NYU CAS people</a>, and 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_NYU_School_of_Medicine_people" title="List of NYU School of Medicine people">List of NYU School of Medicine people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>As the largest private non-profit university in the country, NYU has one of the largest alumni bodies in the world. At the end of 2004, NYU had about 350,000 alumni. Of these, at least 17,000 live abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> The New York University Office for Alumni Affairs oversees various activities such as class reunions, local NYU Club gatherings, NYU alumni travel, and Career Services. The Alumni club on campus is the Torch Club, located in <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a>. In addition, the Princeton Club of New York (PCNY) has also invited New York University alumni for club membership.</p> 
     <p>NYU counts 36 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="Nobel laureates by university affiliation" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Prize winners</a> by affiliation. Notable graduating classes include 1941, which graduated three later <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> laureates (<a href="/wiki/Julius_Axelrod" title="Julius Axelrod">Julius Axelrod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_B._Elion" title="Gertrude B. Elion">Gertrude B. Elion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clifford_Shull" title="Clifford Shull">Clifford Shull</a>), Olympic Gold Medalist <a href="/wiki/John_Woodruff" title="John Woodruff">John Woodruff</a>, sportscaster <a href="/wiki/Howard_Cosell" title="Howard Cosell">Howard Cosell</a> and sociologist <a href="/wiki/Morris_Janowitz" title="Morris Janowitz">Morris Janowitz</a>; 1957 included <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winning author <a href="/wiki/Frank_McCourt" title="Frank McCourt">Frank McCourt</a> and president of <a href="/wiki/Technion-Israel_Institute_of_Technology" title="Technion-Israel Institute of Technology" class="mw-redirect">Technion-Israel Institute of Technology</a> Josef Singer (NYU-Poly); 1970 included <a href="/wiki/Thomas_S._Popkewitz" title="Thomas S. Popkewitz">Thomas S. Popkewitz</a>, professor of curriculum theory at the University of Wisconsin-Madison; 1974 included author <a href="/wiki/Warren_Farrell" title="Warren Farrell">Warren Farrell</a>, Ph.D.; and 1977 included: former <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_System" title="Federal Reserve System">Fed</a> <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Federal_Reserve" title="Chairman of the Federal Reserve">Chairman</a> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Greenspan" title="Alan Greenspan">Alan Greenspan</a>; <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">IRS</a> <a href="/wiki/Commissioner_of_Internal_Revenue" title="Commissioner of Internal Revenue">Commissioner</a> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Everson" title="Mark Everson" class="mw-redirect">Mark Everson</a>; <a href="/wiki/INSEAD" title="INSEAD">INSEAD</a> Dean Gabriel Hawawini; <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Oscar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" title="Tony Award">Tony Award</a> winner <a href="/wiki/John_Patrick_Shanley" title="John Patrick Shanley">John Patrick Shanley</a>; <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a> <a href="/wiki/NHL_Commissioner" title="NHL Commissioner">Commissioner</a> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Bettman" title="Gary Bettman">Gary Bettman</a>; physicist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewis_Earl_Little&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lewis Earl Little (page does not exist)">Lewis E. Little</a>; <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" title="NASDAQ">NASDAQ</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Robert_Greifeld" title="Robert Greifeld">Robert Greifeld</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ma_Ying-jeou" title="Ma Ying-jeou">Ma Ying-jeou</a> president of Republic of China (Taiwan); <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Endara" title="Guillermo Endara">Guillermo Endara</a> president of Republic of Panama, <a href="/wiki/Clive_Davis" title="Clive Davis">Clive Davis</a> music industry executive, and <a href="/wiki/Cathy_Minehan" title="Cathy Minehan">Cathy Minehan</a>, Federal Reserve Chairman Boston. Many <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> companies are currently being headed by NYU-Poly alumni, including <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xerox" title="Xerox">Xerox</a>, and <a href="/wiki/AECOM" title="AECOM">AECOM</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_film_and_literature">In film and literature</span></h2> 
     <p>NYU is often portrayed in a variety of television shows, motion pictures, literature, and other media. Fictional NYU students and faculty include <a href="/wiki/Cosmo_Kramer" title="Cosmo Kramer">Kramer's</a> intern Darren in <i><a href="/wiki/Seinfeld" title="Seinfeld">Seinfeld</a></i>, who helps him run &quot;Kramerica Industries&quot;; a student reporter in a different episode of Seinfeld who interviews <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Seinfeld_(character)" title="Jerry Seinfeld (character)">Jerry</a>; Theo Huxtable (<a href="/wiki/Malcolm-Jamal_Warner" title="Malcolm-Jamal Warner">Malcolm-Jamal Warner</a>) from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cosby_Show" title="The Cosby Show">The Cosby Show</a></i>, who graduates from NYU in the series finale; <a href="/wiki/Ross_Geller" title="Ross Geller">Ross Geller</a> (<a href="/wiki/David_Schwimmer" title="David Schwimmer">David Schwimmer</a>) from <i><a href="/wiki/Friends" title="Friends">Friends</a></i>, who becomes an NYU professor in Season 6; Character Tom Collins from <i><a href="/wiki/Rent_(musical)" title="Rent (musical)">Rent</a></i>, who taught there; Bud Fox (<a href="/wiki/Charlie_Sheen" title="Charlie Sheen">Charlie Sheen</a>) in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_(1987_film)" title="Wall Street (1987 film)">Wall Street</a></i> (1987); Finch (<a href="/wiki/Eddie_Kaye_Thomas" title="Eddie Kaye Thomas">Eddie Kaye Thomas</a>) from the <i><a href="/wiki/American_Pie_(film)" title="American Pie (film)">American Pie</a></i> films; Paul Tannek (<a href="/wiki/Jason_Biggs" title="Jason Biggs">Jason Biggs</a>) in <i><a href="/wiki/Loser_(film)" title="Loser (film)">Loser</a></i> (2000); Alex Foreman (<a href="/wiki/Scarlett_Johansson" title="Scarlett Johansson">Scarlett Johansson</a>) in <i><a href="/wiki/In_Good_Company_(2004_film)" title="In Good Company (2004 film)">In Good Company</a></i> (2005); Jack Campbell (<a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Cage" title="Nicolas Cage">Nicolas Cage</a>) in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Family_Man" title="The Family Man">The Family Man</a></i> (2000); Clark Kellogg (<a href="/wiki/Matthew_Broderick" title="Matthew Broderick">Matthew Broderick</a>) in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Freshman_(1990_film)" title="The Freshman (1990 film)">The Freshman</a></i> (1990); Justin Cobb (<a href="/wiki/Lou_Taylor_Pucci" title="Lou Taylor Pucci">Lou Taylor Pucci</a>) in the film version of <i><a href="/wiki/Thumbsucker_(film)" title="Thumbsucker (film)">Thumbsucker</a></i> (2005), who secretly applies and is accepted to NYU; the songwriter Albert Peterson in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Bye_Bye_Birdie_(musical)" title="Bye Bye Birdie (musical)">Bye Bye Birdie</a></i> who promises his sweetheart Rosie to start studying at NYU and become an English teacher; and the characters <a href="/wiki/Blair_Waldorf" title="Blair Waldorf">Blair Waldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Humphrey" title="Dan Humphrey">Dan Humphrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Abrams" title="Vanessa Abrams">Vanessa Abrams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgina_Sparks" title="Georgina Sparks">Georgina Sparks</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Gossip_Girl_(TV_series)" title="Gossip Girl (TV series)" class="mw-redirect">Gossip Girl</a></i>.</p> 
     <p>In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Campus_of_New_York_University" title="Campus of New York University">campus of NYU</a> has been the backdrop for various pieces of fiction: <a href="/wiki/Grace_Adler" title="Grace Adler">Grace Adler</a>'s office in Will &amp; Grace is portrayed in the show as being in the <a href="/wiki/Puck_Building" title="Puck Building">Puck Building</a>, home to NYU's Wagner School; <a href="/wiki/Henry_James" title="Henry James">Henry James</a>' novel <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_(novel)" title="Washington Square (novel)">Washington Square</a></i> is set around the NYU area; and <i><a href="/wiki/Rose_of_Washington_Square" title="Rose of Washington Square">Rose of Washington Square</a></i> (1939), <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=13_Washington_Square&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="13 Washington Square (page does not exist)">13 Washington Square</a></i> (1928), <i><a href="/wiki/Annie_Hall" title="Annie Hall">Annie Hall</a></i> (1977), <i><a href="/wiki/When_Harry_Met_Sally" title="When Harry Met Sally" class="mw-redirect">When Harry Met Sally</a></i> (1989), <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Legend_(film)" title="I Am Legend (film)">I Am Legend</a></i> (2007), <i><a href="/wiki/August_Rush" title="August Rush">August Rush</a></i> (2007), <i><a href="/wiki/Remember_Me_(2010_film)" title="Remember Me (2010 film)">Remember Me</a></i> (2010), <i><a href="/wiki/Step_Up_3-D" title="Step Up 3-D" class="mw-redirect">Step Up 3-D</a></i> (2010) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sorcerer%27s_Apprentice_(2010_film)" title="The Sorcerer's Apprentice (2010 film)">The Sorcerer's Apprentice</a></i> (2010) are centered around the NYU campus. In <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Bakshi" title="Ralph Bakshi">Ralph Bakshi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Animated_film" title="Animated film" class="mw-redirect">animated feature</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Fritz_the_Cat_(film)" title="Fritz the Cat (film)">Fritz The Cat</a></i> (1972), the dormitory that Fritz burns down is clearly supposed to be NYU's Weinstein Hall, located at 5-11 University Place near the northeast corner of <a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_Park,_New_York" title="Washington Square Park, New York" class="mw-redirect">Washington Square Park</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Warner_Brothers" title="Warner Brothers" class="mw-redirect">Warner Brothers</a> show <i><a href="/wiki/Felicity_(TV_series)" title="Felicity (TV series)">Felicity</a></i> was set at the &quot;University of New York&quot;, clearly modeled after NYU; and NYU's old University Heights Campus in the Bronx provided the scenery for <i><a href="/wiki/Sophie%27s_Choice_(film)" title="Sophie's Choice (film)">Sophie's Choice</a></i> (1982), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Thomas_Crown_Affair_(1999_film)" title="The Thomas Crown Affair (1999 film)">The Thomas Crown Affair</a></i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/A_Beautiful_Mind_(film)" title="A Beautiful Mind (film)">A Beautiful Mind</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/Maid_in_Manhattan" title="Maid in Manhattan">Maid in Manhattan</a></i> (2002), <i><a href="/wiki/Mona_Lisa_Smile" title="Mona Lisa Smile">Mona Lisa Smile</a></i> (2003), and <i><a href="/wiki/Step_Up_3D" title="Step Up 3D">Step Up 3D</a></i> (2010). NYU is also featured in the TV show <i><a href="/wiki/Californication_(TV_series)" title="Californication (TV series)">Californication</a></i>.</p>
